  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f2087890-f78b-48f9-bfac-6d1e210ab489'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer715030155976881607">All Stevie Bell wanted was to find the key to the Ellingham mystery, but instead she found her classmate dead. And while she solved that murder, the crimes of the past are still waiting in the dark. Just as Stevie feels she’s on the cusp of putting it together, her parents pull her out of Ellingham academy.<br/><br/>For her own safety they say. She must move past this obsession with</span>
  <span id="freeText715030155976881607" style="display:none">All Stevie Bell wanted was to find the key to the Ellingham mystery, but instead she found her classmate dead. And while she solved that murder, the crimes of the past are still waiting in the dark. Just as Stevie feels she’s on the cusp of putting it together, her parents pull her out of Ellingham academy.<br /><br />For her own safety they say. She must move past this obsession with crime. Now that Stevie’s away from the school of topiaries and secret tunnels, and her strange and endearing friends, she begins to feel disconnected from the rest of the world. At least she won’t have to see David anymore. David, who she kissed. David, who lied to her about his identity—son of despised politician Edward King. Then King himself arrives at her house to offer a deal: He will bring Stevie back to Ellingham immediately. In return, she must play nice with David. King is in the midst of a campaign and can’t afford his son stirring up trouble. If Stevie’s at school, David will stay put.<br /><br />The tantalizing riddles behind the Ellingham murders are still waiting to be unraveled, and Stevie knows she’s so close. But the path to the truth has more twists and turns than she can imagine—and moving forward involves hurting someone she cares for. In New York Times bestselling author Maureen Johnson’s second novel of the <i>Truly Devious</i> series, nothing is free, and someone will pay for the truth with their life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="715030155976881607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1511630-why-does-maureen-johnson-always-refer-to">Why does Maureen Johnson always refer to Vi as &quot;they&quot; and never &quot;her&quot;? This really bothers me. &quot;Vi had a can of dark spray they were going to lend Stevie for her hair.&quot; &quot;Vi walked up to Stevie and they gave her a hug.&quot; I don&#39;t understand this. it&#39;s only with this character. Am I missing something? Is she a siamese twin?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1511630'><a id="like_count_community_question_1511630" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1511630?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">4 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F39893545-the-vanishing-stair">like</a></span>

</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/37016646-daphne"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1592518336i/37016646._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/37016646-daphne">Daphne</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
They/them are Vi's chosen pronouns. Janelle corrects Stevie about this in the first book at some point, I believe.
</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4836217660564107415">WOWOWOW I loved this book so much!! A fantastic sequel, possibly even more enjoyable than the first installment, which was tough to beat.<br/> <br/>CW: anxiety/panic attacks, murder, death, abduction<br/> <br/>I came away from <i>The Vanishing Stair</i> with such a greater appreciation for this entire series.   <span id="freeText4836217660564107415" style="display:none">WOWOWOW I loved this book so much!! A fantastic sequel, possibly even more enjoyable than the first installment, which was tough to beat.<br /> <br />CW: anxiety/panic attacks, murder, death, abduction<br /> <br />I came away from <i>The Vanishing Stair</i> with such a greater appreciation for this entire series. From the impeccable characterization to the flawlessly constructed plot, <i>The Vanishing Stair</i> is everything one would want from a second installment. It’s not as if anything was lacking in <i>Truly Devious</i>, but the sequel made me fall in more in love with every aspect of this story.<br /><br />The mystery really takes an unexpected turn in this novel, going in a direction I had not expected and leaving me wanting more. It is truly difficult to predict the many twists and turns that make this one of the greatest young adult mysteries I have ever read.<br /><br />I cannot recommend this series enough! If you have yet to start it, you are in for a real treat.<br /><br /><i>This book was sent to me unsolicited and for free by HarperTeen. I had no obligation to review this book and all opinions are my own.</i></span>

<div id="review_2603605602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2603605602" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2603605602?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-thriller-mystery">ya-thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-ff-side">lgbtq-ff-side</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2603605602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14010345865239950771">How am I supposed to....go on being a person after that ending?<br/><br/>Let me preface this by stating that this entire review could be replaced by a footage of me striding down a big hallway in a fancy period gown yelling “fuck fuck fuck” because that would more accurately sum up all my feelings.<br/><br/><u>
  
    <strong>So, what’s this book about?</strong>
  
</u><br/><br/>Stevie is cast away from the Ellingham academy by her parents and promptly ordered to push the sour remains of her time in Ellingham to the back of her mind. But Stevie’s m</span>
  <span id="freeText14010345865239950771" style="display:none">How am I supposed to....go on being a person after that ending?<br /><br />Let me preface this by stating that this entire review could be replaced by a footage of me striding down a big hallway in a fancy period gown yelling “fuck fuck fuck” because that would more accurately sum up all my feelings.<br /><br /><u>
  
    <strong>So, what’s this book about?</strong>
  
</u><br /><br />Stevie is cast away from the Ellingham academy by her parents and promptly ordered to push the sour remains of her time in Ellingham to the back of her mind. But Stevie’s mind is still awhirl with thoughts and memories, and, at the center of everything: the mystery of “Truly, Devious”. She’d gone looking for answers, and gotten none, and the puzzle wouldn’t let her go. Now her friend is missing, one of her classmates is dead and When Edward King, the abhorrent politician Stevie’s parents work for, offers her a private jet ride to the academy in exchange of keeping his son in line, Stevie doesn’t hesitate before she claws at the offer with both hands.<br /><br />Stevie thought she could catch the mystery of Ellingham like fireflies in a jar, but the enormity of it soon reaches out to catch her. Now she’s churned under the horrid sense that fate was hunting and had already picked out its quarry.<br /><br />I finished this book with the sudden urge to <em>pace</em>, bitter and frantic and feeling every second of my frustration and deprivation. It was almost unbearable to come so close to getting answers, to barely feel and almost taste before being snatched away and left to walk the circle of my own thoughts, which centered partly on the question of: who the <em>hell</em> was the first person to invent the concept of cliffhangers and have they ever issued a public apology?<br /><br /><strong>I really loved this book.</strong> I read it in one sitting, the hours trickling past unnoticed, and silence reigning, broken only by the shush of pages turning. <em>The Vanishing Stair</em> is immaculately plotted and a real page-turner. It’s outstandingly enjoyable and addictive. The author craftily takes on two timelines, two chilling mysteries with truly elusive solutions, multiple deaths and supports all of that with engaging characters and a strong action-thriller backbone. The result is a remarkably smooth narrative experience.<br /><br />This sequel really outdid its predecessor. Secrets swell to bursting, tension rises, the pace picks up, dread lances through every moment until the story ends abruptly and leaves you panting for more. <strong>I was completely riveted.</strong> The characters dig up the past, push for answers, tip the dominoes, and alongside them, burning threads were racing through my mind, connecting far-flung dots and filling in blanks, erasing question marks and adding a dozen more for every one erased, before the truth is unraveled and recognition sparks, sharp as a shock.<br /><br />I love Stevie’s character and how she often blurs the line between caution and daring, unwilling to yield to the tiresome compromise that striking balance between the two tends to be. She doesn’t dwell on the possibility that her ambition to solve a centuries-old mystery may lay far beyond her talent, instead, she accelerates towards doom and peril without thinking ahead of the repercussions. It’s pretty fun to spend time inside her head. I’ve also grown so fond of the cast of characters. Nate, especially, is my absolute favorite. If I were a fictional character, I’d totally be him: he’s extremely introverted, has zero conversational skills, represses emotional trauma, is unimpressed by the risks the main characters are taking because, and I quote, “why. do. people. do. stupid. things,” and will probably still be alive by the end of the series. New characters are introduced as well, demanding the spotlight for themselves and leading to further entanglements,  like the eccentric Dr. Irene Fenton who wrote about the Ellingham murders and recruits Stevie’s help to further her research.<br /><br />I think my one and only quibble with this book is that I wanted more page time with David and Stevie. Their relationship has grown fraught with the untold weight of their secrets and I just wanted to grab them both by the shoulders and scream: “PLEASE <em>COMMUNICATE</em>.”<br /><br />Overall, <em>The Vanishing Stair</em> was an immensely engrossing and rollicking experience and I can’t wait for the story to drag out all its secrets in the next and final installment!<br /><br /><b>4,5 stars</b><br /><br /><a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">BLOG</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">TWITTER</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/runawaywithdreamthieves" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a> | <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">TUMBLR</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14010345865239950771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2443241109" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2443241109" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2443241109?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2443241109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9825278349249629870"><b>**4.5-stars**</b><br/><br/>Dearest Maureen Johnson,<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595523685ra/29856185.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>First, how dare you?</b><br/><br/>It was <i>truly devious</i> of you to hit me with <u>YET ANOTHER</u> cliffhanger ending!<br/><br/>Nevertheless, I will continue to read anything you ever choose to write.<br/><br/>Love you like a friend,<br/><br/>Megs<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566764823ra/28050379.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I had many, many thoughts whilst reading this.<br/> <br/>For example, there was this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428547791ra/14443820.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Followed by this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457182726ra/18329371.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Wrapped up by this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1556149896ra/27409732.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In all seriousness though, that ending!?!?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1556923431ra/27451895.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I <u>really wasn't expecting that</u>, even though Ms. Johnson has played me like that before.<br/><br/>I was totally invested in this</span>
  <span id="freeText9825278349249629870" style="display:none"><b>**4.5-stars**</b><br><br>Dearest Maureen Johnson,<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595523685ra/29856185.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>First, how dare you?</b><br><br>It was <i>truly devious</i> of you to hit me with <u>YET ANOTHER</u> cliffhanger ending!<br><br>Nevertheless, I will continue to read anything you ever choose to write.<br><br>Love you like a friend,<br><br>Megs<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566764823ra/28050379.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I had many, many thoughts whilst reading this.<br> <br>For example, there was this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428547791ra/14443820.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Followed by this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457182726ra/18329371.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wrapped up by this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1556149896ra/27409732.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In all seriousness though, that ending!?!?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1556923431ra/27451895.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I <u>really wasn't expecting that</u>, even though Ms. Johnson has played me like that before.<br><br>I was totally invested in this story. I loved being back with Stevie and the rest of the cast at Ellingham Academy. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589995338ra/29511247.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We meet some new characters and a few more pieces of the puzzle are filled in. I really enjoyed the cold case aspect of the story once again. <br><br>Alternating timelines between past and present is an aspect I always seem to enjoy. I feel like it keeps me more engaged, at times, than a single, linear narrative would.<br><br>If you enjoyed the first book, I think you will enjoy this one as well. Honestly though, I did not love this quite as much. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473858537ra/20523325.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think part of my swooning over <i>Truly Devious</i> was being new to Ellingham Academy and learning about the school, its history and all of the people living there. We had less of that excitement in this one, at least for me.<br><br>Does this book suffer from the dreaded 'middle book syndrome'?<br><br>Maybe, a little.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496828604ra/22955474.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Calm down, not much, just a teeny-tiny bit.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486533392ra/21924271.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am completely stoked for the conclusion to this trilogy and will definitely be preordering it to add to my bookshelves!<br><br><u>Side Note:</u> Really hoping the cover is a nice, deep green. That would make my Slytherin heart so damn happy.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1556923431ra/27451894.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9825278349249629870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2735846588" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2735846588" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2735846588?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735846588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4873102181295291220">you know that feeling when you misremember how you felt about a book, potentially romanticising it, because you swear the story was just that good?? i think i did that with <i>‘truly devious’</i> because i went into this expecting it to be a five star read. and maybe thats my fault. i should have done a quick reread beforehand because this sequel did nothing to help me remember why i thought i was obsessed with this story. <br/><br/>dont get me wrong. its still a pretty solid sequel and a really good book, but i</span>
  <span id="freeText4873102181295291220" style="display:none">you know that feeling when you misremember how you felt about a book, potentially romanticising it, because you swear the story was just that good?? i think i did that with <i>‘truly devious’</i> because i went into this expecting it to be a five star read. and maybe thats my fault. i should have done a quick reread beforehand because this sequel did nothing to help me remember why i thought i was obsessed with this story. <br /><br />dont get me wrong. its still a pretty solid sequel and a really good book, but it didnt live up to my unfairly high expectations. what i enjoyed most was that i kept wanting to turn the page. MJ has perfected the art of subtle giving - just enough to keep the reader satisfied, while also making them want more. the pacing is really good, there is never a dull moment, and i thought the story did a great job at picking up where the previous book left off.<br /><br />however, there is a pretty big reveal in this book, one that readers have been dying to know since the beginning, and i was very underwhelmed with it. its one of those reveals that the reader would never guess because it kind of comes out of nowhere, with none of the given hints leading to it. so thats a bit of a bummer. <br /><br />but overall this is a fun and exciting book. definitely not as good as the first one (based on how i remember it), but still very much worth my time. im looking forward to seeing how things get wrapped up in the concluding instalment! <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4873102181295291220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2772567107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14795796092063157474">I can’t remember anything that happened in this book.<br/><br/>Judging by my pre-review (which consists of about one-third expletives and three-thirds surprise), I was shocked by something. I do not remember what that thing was, but considering this is a murder mystery, and also the second book in a series, I’m going to guess it was one part Big Reveal and one part cliffhanger.<br/><br/>How frustrating, presumably, for past me.<br/><br/>The only thing I really remember is finding this book slightly disappointing in compariso</span>
  <span id="freeText14795796092063157474" style="display:none">I can’t remember anything that happened in this book.<br /><br />Judging by my pre-review (which consists of about one-third expletives and three-thirds surprise), I was shocked by something. I do not remember what that thing was, but considering this is a murder mystery, and also the second book in a series, I’m going to guess it was one part Big Reveal and one part cliffhanger.<br /><br />How frustrating, presumably, for past me.<br /><br />The only thing I really remember is finding this book slightly disappointing in comparison to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555916573" rel="nofollow noopener">the first one</a>. Not by a lot, just a half-star or so.<br /><br />I can assume I had some of the same issues with it I had with the first one: weird pacing due to this being a trilogy about one or two mysteries; an overwhelming onslaught of quirkiness. Also, something I loved about the first one was Boarding School, and this one consisted of way more time spent off-campus, leading to kind of a last-book-in-Harry-Potter-can’t-they-just-stay-at-Hogwarts type feel.<br /><br />And we all know how I felt about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1115588640?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Deathly Hallows</a>.<br /><br />But in the end, I have to assume that my main issue is the one I can recall with the most clarity:<br /><br />I don’t remember jack sh*t about it.<br /><br />Looks like I’ll have to reread this ahead of the next book.<br /><br />Bottom line: ??? Also, why do I have to WAIT SO DAMN LONG. I am not patient enough for this.<br /><br />--------<br /><br />it is with great sincerity and the utmost respect that i must say:<br /><br />WHAT THE FUCK???!!! what the fuck<br /><br /><br />(rtc / 3 stars)<br />--------<br /><br />started reading this as close to "immediately upon finishing the first book" as was physically possible for me</span>

<div id="review_2468379360" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2468379360" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2468379360?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2468379360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17341694994992885776"><b>I. LOVED. THIS. SO. FREAKIN. MUCH</b><br/><br/>This was ... WILD. The twists?!?! The turns!!! The REVEALS. I think this is definitely becoming one of my new favourite series?? and I am DYING FOR BOOK THREE ALREADY<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>Where do you look for someone who's never really there? Always on a staircase, but never on a stair.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>The Vanishing Stair starts a few months after the events of Truly Devious. Despite being pulled from Ellingham Academy by her parents, the mysteries of Ellingham Academy and the Truly Devious case </span>
  <span id="freeText17341694994992885776" style="display:none"><b>I. LOVED. THIS. SO. FREAKIN. MUCH</b><br><br>This was ... WILD. The twists?!?! The turns!!! The REVEALS. I think this is definitely becoming one of my new favourite series?? and I am DYING FOR BOOK THREE ALREADY<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>Where do you look for someone who's never really there? Always on a staircase, but never on a stair.</blockquote>
</i><br><br>The Vanishing Stair starts a few months after the events of Truly Devious. Despite being pulled from Ellingham Academy by her parents, the mysteries of Ellingham Academy and the Truly Devious case still haunt Stevie. So she makes a deal with the devil (Edward King) and returns to Ellingham - in exchange for watching out for David, who she hasn't talked to since she left. But despite holding a fresh clue into the Truly Devious case, it seems harder than ever to solve - what does the new clue mean, what happened to Ellie, and how does the girl and boy who Stevie found in the photos tie back into the case.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554792335i/27334808.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>Maureen Johnson absolutely outdid herself with this one! I enjoyed it even more than book one, which was one of my favourite books of 2018. <br><br>The Vanishing Stair was just as twisty and compelling as I expected. We're almost immediately thrown back into the mystery of Truly Devious and this book flew past for me. I finished the large majority of it in one sitting because it was so compelling and the time just flew past as I was reading it. I was totally immersed in the world, the characters, the mystery and everything. <br><br>I love the aesthetics of these book so much. The dark academia feel / mysterious boarding school element is an absolute favourite of mine. WE NEED MORE OF THIS !! This book is also kinda gory at times? And creepy? And ooh boy I loved that so much !! (Even though I was lowkey worrying about people appearing at the end of my bed as I was trying to sleep after finishing this)<br><br>I also LOVED HOW THE MYSTERY PLAYED OUT. I don't wanna reveal too much because spoilers, but <b>Maureen Johnson reveals so much, and yet it doesn't answer anything - it just leads to more questions</b> and I thought that was SO INTERESTING !! I loved how the mystery expanded and became even more thorny and strange. I also loved how many clues we're given, and there is a chance to put it all together alongside Stevie (though of course I didn't because I am a dumb dumb). And that ending .. KILLED ME. And you know what? I love a good cliffhanger. Yes they're awful but they're also THE BEST. They get me so hyped for the next book and let me tell you ... 2020 needs to come faster because I am HYPED. <br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554792335i/27334807.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><b>lets talk characters</b><br><br>I really enjoyed Stevie in this once again! She is a super intriguing character to follow and I love how fleshed out she is. The representation of her mental illness is also really well done, and I related to a lot of the things about anxiety. <br><br>I do wish Janelle and Nate had been in this more. Especially Janelle and Vi, they are such cute girlfriends and we need more of them. But I enjoyed the new side characters. Those being, the two students in 1929 introduced as part of the mystery. Both those characters were intriguing and I hope we learn more about them in the last book.<br><br>My surprise stand out favourite was .. the romance!? Now I don't usually care much for romance subplots but I am FEELING THIS ONE. The miscommunication was kind of annoying, but overall I am really, really into David/Stevie and like ,, actually felt my cold dead heart move a little every time they talked. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>"There's nothing more deceptive than an obvious fact." <br>
</blockquote>
</i><br><br>OVERALL, I LOVED THIS SO MUCH. I really hope more people pick up this series! I think it is so fun, so well written and has all that dark academia / creepy boarding school / mysterious aesthetic I know yall are hard for. @ the publisher if you're listening ................ send me book 3. (Actual rating 4.5*)<br><br>tws: anxiety/panic attacks, murder, death, abduction, dissections</span>
  <a data-text-id="17341694994992885776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2678837659?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2678837659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2896768981946265542"> This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/02/05/the-vanishing-stair-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/> <i>“Where do you look for someone who’s never really there? Always on a staircase but never on a stair.” </i><br/><br/>🌟 The Vanishing Stair was what I expected it to be; an unnecessary bridge to the third book and this whole series could have been a duology. Yes, this book fell into the second book syndrome with much blabber and not much happening till the end!<br/><br/>🌟 I enjoyed book 1 more than I did with this one because there were much </span>
  <span id="freeText2896768981946265542" style="display:none"> This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/02/05/the-vanishing-stair-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /> <i>“Where do you look for someone who’s never really there? Always on a staircase but never on a stair.” </i><br /><br />🌟 The Vanishing Stair was what I expected it to be; an unnecessary bridge to the third book and this whole series could have been a duology. Yes, this book fell into the second book syndrome with much blabber and not much happening till the end!<br /><br />🌟 I enjoyed book 1 more than I did with this one because there were much to explore in it and not much to do so here! I read the 2 books in January so I didn’t have to go through that excruciating waiting that most of readers went through. I was slightly disappointed with how things carried on from the start. After the ending of book 1, you would expect a better beginning than the one this book had.<br /><br />🌟 My feelings toward the characters did not change, I am not a big fan of any of them but I stand corrected on one point; I mentioned on my review of book 1 that the characters should be better given that it is a school for the best of the best. I don’t know how it escaped my attention but really, most of the students in the school were there as friends of the owner or they are connected to him in that way whether in the past or present!<br /><br />🌟 There wasn’t much happening and I got bored, the last chapters were good and maybe it is because things finally happened then and we got an explanation to one of the mysteries.<br /><br />🌟 Summary: This book was like book 1 in terms of characters, writing and the world-building. Less happened but we got ourselves some answers at last. I am not convinced in the contemporary/ Mystery mix but I am willing to read the last book when it is out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2896768981946265542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2672040108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2672040108" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2672040108?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2672040108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5823192193565922436">Four more astonishing and intriguing, TG this time I’m not disappointed stars! <br/><br/>This book’s difference from the first one, we don’t need any introductions about Ellingham academy, its history and past kidnapping, murder mysteries. It started where it left and we have some revelations, more informations, finding important pieces of puzzle. <br/>This is more fast paced, riveting and entertaining book. I even start to empathize Stevie, her techniques, her obsessions, way of thinking, emotional up and dow</span>
  <span id="freeText5823192193565922436" style="display:none">Four more astonishing and intriguing, TG this time I’m not disappointed stars! <br /><br />This book’s difference from the first one, we don’t need any introductions about Ellingham academy, its history and past kidnapping, murder mysteries. It started where it left and we have some revelations, more informations, finding important pieces of puzzle. <br />This is more fast paced, riveting and entertaining book. I even start to empathize Stevie, her techniques, her obsessions, way of thinking, emotional up and downs. <br />The characters are still so much quirky, emotionally unstable but they’re smart, unique and entertaining in some ways ! I still like Nate and I got used to his antics! Still have big questions about David but as soon as he made a clean slate and told the truths about his f*cked up family history, I started to understand the sources of his mean and douchebag attitudes. <br /><br />This time, there is a real cliffhanger at the end and we finally learned the kidnappers’ identities but it resulted with more unanswered questions! We’re still in the dark about student murders and perpetrators! <br /><br />So looking forward to read the end of the trilogy! This is not the best YA murder mysteries that I’ve ever read! But it’s still brilliant and the way of storytelling, the references of old Doyle and Christie books makes you satisfied and keep your attention! <br /><br />I wish I started to read them after the releasing of final book. Now I have to wait at least six months! That’s the worst thing when you finally get attached to a story, characters and the writing style of the author! Damn!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5823192193565922436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9164096270391390200">The most disappointing part of the book?! The 'Acknowledgwments' just after the last chapter! I wanted MORE...and yes, I can imagine how vampires must be craving for warm blood to survive.<br/>Ok, for Nate's sake, how this book made my life incompletely complete:<br/>The second book started with a bang!   <span id="freeText9164096270391390200" style="display:none">The most disappointing part of the book?! The 'Acknowledgwments' just after the last chapter! I wanted MORE...and yes, I can imagine how vampires must be craving for warm blood to survive.<br />Ok, for Nate's sake, how this book made my life incompletely complete:<br />The second book started with a bang! Each page was so entertaining, except for the David parts, of course. (I still cannot get used to this character nor to the awkward romance. I guess I never will.) I find almost every character really amusing. Each character introduced had a mystery. Things might appear simple and fun but the real fun began when the book was just about to end. One mystery gets solved, three or four mysteries jump up just like that (and we all know how we love to get our lives ruined when the book ends with cliffhangers). <br />There's still some three or more murder mysteries yet to get solved and one very important mystery that had started it all still looming large. <br /><br />The second book is much more fast paced, packed with action and some pulse throbbing case solving adventure! Secrets, hidden answers, trust matters, weird characters.....gave me more than what I had anticipated.<br />I just don't like the awkward romance thing between David and Stevie. It's so awkward. I preferred the chemistry between Vi and Janelle more no matter how small their parts were. In fact, I like all the characters with all their flaws and perfections.<br />Looking past the weakest character and chemistry issue, the book is still a solid 5 star read!<br /><br />I appreciate the Agatha Christie, Sherlock Holmes and Edgar Allan Poe references!<br /><br />Such a good nerdy read I was craving for!<br /><br />😈 Hey, third book, you cannot do anything but get ready to get stuck with me for the next two hours or so eh?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9164096270391390200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2893764044" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2893764044" />
    <a title="Mackenzie Lane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26303598-mackenzie-lane"><img alt="Mackenzie Lane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559203827p2/26303598.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2893764044?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mackenzie Lane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mackenzie Lane" href="/user/show/26303598-mackenzie-lane">Mackenzie Lane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26303598-mackenzie-lane?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26303598-mackenzie-lane?shelf=ya-mystery-thriller">ya-mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2893764044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9580558247131422717"><b>The plot thickens.</b><br/><br/>Now that's what I call a cliff-hanger! So much was revealed in the last 50 pages, and for it to end like that? <i>Bravo</i>, Maureen Johnson.<br/><br/>I definitely enjoyed this second novel in the Truly Devious series more than the first. It still carried all the luscious descriptions of crisp Autumn mornings that I so loved in <i>Truly Devious</i>; I'll never tire of reading about fall in New England. <br/><br/>The characters felt worn-in, in the best way possible. Nate is my favorite, by far. David's still we</span>
  <span id="freeText9580558247131422717" style="display:none"><b>The plot thickens.</b><br /><br />Now that's what I call a cliff-hanger! So much was revealed in the last 50 pages, and for it to end like that? <i>Bravo</i>, Maureen Johnson.<br /><br />I definitely enjoyed this second novel in the Truly Devious series more than the first. It still carried all the luscious descriptions of crisp Autumn mornings that I so loved in <i>Truly Devious</i>; I'll never tire of reading about fall in New England. <br /><br />The characters felt worn-in, in the best way possible. Nate is my favorite, by far. David's still weird. Stevie's still Stevie. But we were also introduced to a few new characters! Fun, fun. <br /><br />I'm so happy we finally got concrete answers toward the Ellingham case. I won't spoil anything, but I was genuinely perplexed as to who the kidnapper was. <br /><br />The first half of the book felt like nothing was really happening, and that's because nothing was really happening. I did appreciate, however, the recap of the events from the first novel. It was a thorough recap, but never tedious. <br /><br />I'm very much looking forward to seeing how everything wraps up in the third book! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9580558247131422717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17813407773162173762"><p>
  <a href='https://onethousandandonebook.wordpress.com/2019/01/29/a-poem-review-the-vanishing-stair-truly-devious-2-by-maureen-johnson/#more-270' rel='nofollow noopener'>**This review now posted on my blog**</a>
  <br/>
</p><p>Dear readers, may I present you a <i>desperate</i> attempt of a <i>bad poet</i> with a <i>shitty rhyme</i> at expressing her WTF feelings aimed at <i>The Vanishing Stair</i> aka <i>The Torture Device</i> aka <i>one more year of desolation</i> aka <i>nine circles of hell</i> aka-- You get the picture! <br/><br/><b><i>Riddle riddle on the wall, who's the wickedest of them all?<br/>You are wicked, there's no doubt.<br/>But the slyest of them all is Maureen Johnson!<br/><br/>Riddle riddle on the wall, how do I survive the fall?<br/>Under stair </i></b></p></span>
  <span id="freeText17813407773162173762" style="display:none"><p>
  <a href="https://onethousandandonebook.wordpress.com/2019/01/29/a-poem-review-the-vanishing-stair-truly-devious-2-by-maureen-johnson/#more-270" rel="nofollow noopener">**This review now posted on my blog**</a>
  <br />
</p><p>Dear readers, may I present you a <i>desperate</i> attempt of a <i>bad poet</i> with a <i>shitty rhyme</i> at expressing her WTF feelings aimed at <i>The Vanishing Stair</i> aka <i>The Torture Device</i> aka <i>one more year of desolation</i> aka <i>nine circles of hell</i> aka-- You get the picture! <br /><br /><b><i>Riddle riddle on the wall, who's the wickedest of them all?<br />You are wicked, there's no doubt.<br />But the slyest of them all is Maureen Johnson!<br /><br />Riddle riddle on the wall, how do I survive the fall?<br />Under stair and straight to hell<br />Do I beg or scream or kill?<br />You will fall, there's no doubt.<br />Brace yourself and get a knife.<br /><br />Riddle riddle on the wall, what the fuck is going on?<br />The truth is close, there's no doubt.<br />But you're too dumb to get the hint!<br /><br />Riddle riddle on the wall, do you tell the truth at all?!<br />Truth or dare, which one'd be fair?<br />Heart attack or puzzle slain?<br />Curiosity's a hit! Cat will eat it in one seat!<br />If you want to know the truth, wait another year to choose!<br />Haha.</i></b><br /><br /><i>Dear readers, if you fell victims of this <s>riddle</s> book as I did, please contact me down below in the comments to discuss a revenge plan on it.</i><br /><br />Yours,<br />truly dead</p></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer7317075064578872707"><u>
  <b>Actual Rating: ⭐⭐⭐⭐.5</b>
</u><br/><br/><i>
  <b>"Where do you look for someone who's never really there?<br/>Always on a staircase but never on a stair."</b>
</i><br/><br/>DID IT SERIOUSLY JUST END LIKE <b>THAT???!!!</b><br/>Wow.😠<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593719010ra/29752193.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Just wow. Someone should seriously congratulate Maureen Johnson with her amazing cliffhangers. <br/><br/><b><u>WARNING: SPOILERS BELOW FROM BOOK 1!!!! (spoilers from this book are in tags)</u><br/><i>You have been warned</i>............</b><br/><br/>I thought <b>Truly Devious's</b> ending was bad but no...........this is <b>WAY</b> worse.<br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Again, I never thought George </span></span>
  <span id="freeText7317075064578872707" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>Actual Rating: ⭐⭐⭐⭐.5</b>
</u><br><br><i>
  <b>"Where do you look for someone who's never really there?<br>Always on a staircase but never on a stair."</b>
</i><br><br>DID IT SERIOUSLY JUST END LIKE <b>THAT???!!!</b><br>Wow.😠<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593719010ra/29752193.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Just wow. Someone should seriously congratulate Maureen Johnson with her amazing cliffhangers. <br><br><b><u>WARNING: SPOILERS BELOW FROM BOOK 1!!!! (spoilers from this book are in tags)</u><br><i>You have been warned</i>............</b><br><br>I thought <b>Truly Devious's</b> ending was bad but no...........this is <b>WAY</b> worse.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Again, I never thought George Marsh would be the one behind the Truly Devious case. He really did seem like a good friend of Ellingham. But they do say never trust anyone during a case, especially if they're close to you.<br>And I can't believe that two students came up with the Truly Devious letter as a prank and in the end that prank just complicated the investigation 75 years after. Frankie and Edward are actually geniuses, though they obviously didn't think it'd turn so serious. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Honestly, I would be such a bad detective.😅 I see Stevie saying that she's figured it all out and I'm just like.......wait who is it???? <br><br>And then after Stevie figured out that Ellie was the murderer of Hayes and had escaped, I thought that they'd eventually track her down and find Ellie, but no..........it was <b>much deeper</b> than that. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ellie hadn't even left Ellingham this whole time and was hiding underground, but when Stevie and David found her body, she was dead.........which makes me wonder.........was she really the one who killed Hayes? I feel like maybe she had something to do with the murder but I don't think she intended for Hayes to die or something? <br>Also, I know she has to be guilty of something because she ran away and I don't believe that she ran away from fear, but I think it wasn't really fear of being put into jail but maybe something bigger than that. She might be working with powerful people who might do something to her if she talked. Haha Idk. Maybe I'm thinking too much into it or completely off. I do wonder tho........🤔 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>There are SO MANY suspicious people in this book, that I think I've just decided to not trust them all. Everyone's a suspect now (minus the crew cuz I really don't think they have anything to do with this). David is also being really suspicious but I don't think he has anything to do with the murders, though I could be wrong. I mean, I didn't think Ellie was evil, but look at how that turned out😕.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[HUNTER IS DEFINITELY ON MY SUSPECTS LIST. I thought it was Dr. Fenton but she's dead now (or at least that's how the book ended) so she can't be a suspect anymore. Right.....? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Honestly, this whole thing is confusing. I'm so not cut out for detective work. I'll leave that to Stevie.😎<br><br>Oh and every time I see Albert Ellingham talking about how much he loves games, I just picture an mischievous smile on his face—maybe even <b>
  <i>evil</i>
</b>.😨<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593720837ra/29752294.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Scary pikachu..........</b> *shudder*<br><br>Also, I don't know if it's just me but Edward King reminds me a lot of Donald Trump. I was wondering before why Stevie hated the politician so much, but now......I completely understand your hatred Stevie.😔<br><br><i>
  <b>"Edward King was the worst man in America.<br>Well, that point could be argued. But Edward King was a powerful man. He was a Pennsylvania senator, based here, out of Pittsburgh. This was the man who wanted to keep “outsiders” and “bad elements” out of America, which largely meant people who weren’t white, weren’t rich. For Edward King, wealth was goodness. There was no climate change in his world—the earth was there to produce more life-affirming dollars. This was a man who wanted to be president."</b>
</i><br><br>I swear this sounds exactly like Trump🤣 Especially the 'there's no such thing as climate change'.<br><br>Also, David is still.........well, let's just stay that I still don't like him. He really annoys me. Although, I've gotta say that he is funny, if crazy.<br><br><i>
  <b>“Tell her about the screaming,” Janelle said. “Because I can’t.”<br><br>“The screaming?” Stevie repeated.<br><br>“The other morning he started something called ‘screaming meditation,’” Nate said. “Guess what happens in screaming meditation? Did you guess screaming? For fifteen minutes? Because that’s what happens in screaming meditation. Fifteen. Minutes. Outside. At five in the morning. Do you know what happens when someone screams outside for fifteen minutes at five in the morning at a remote location in the mountains, especially after a . . .”<br><br>The implied dot dot dot was “student dies in a terrible accident or maybe murder and another one goes missing.”<br><br>“When security got to him he claimed it was his new religion and that it is something he needs to do every morning now as a way to talk to the sun.”</b>
</i><br><br>Ahhh David was really not okay in this book.🤣 <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And now he's run off and away from Ellingham. RIP David. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Nate as always, was awesome. I seriously love this guy so much. He literally just speaks his mind and was even said to be the only smart one in the group. He's almost always with Stevie on her investigations and like Stevie can confide with Nate on the big stuff. He was like the first person to hear from Stevie that she'd figured out the Truly Devious case. Nate🥰<br><br><i>
  <b>“. . . the last few weeks have been a time of such sadness. What you need to know, what you must know, is that your safety, your health, your emotional well-being is what matters the most. We are going to be here for you. We’re going to have . . .”<br><br>“Counselors,” Nate mumbled under his breath. “You get a counselor and you get a counselor, and you get . . .”</b>
</i><br><br>He's so annoyed.😂<br><br>And Dottie. I love how even though she knew there was something wrong and was super scared, she was still able to think straight and leave a clue in her Sherlock Holmes novel. No way would I have ever thought of that. I would've been way too terrified to move if I knew I was probably about to die. She's got guts. Especially trying to escape afterwards right in front of the murderer <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Curse you George Marsh for killing Dottie. She was a nice girl😥 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I'm deciding whether I should just wait for the library copy of <b>The Hand on the Wall</b> or be impatient and read the ebook.😅 I have no idea what to do.🤷‍♀️<br><br><b>
  <a href="https://chainofnovels.wordpress.com/2020/07/28/the-vanishing-stair-truly-devious-2-spoiler-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">|Blog|</a>
</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7317075064578872707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3016947947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11370717499749459616"><b>First Read: October 2019, Rating: 4 stars<br/>Second Read: November 2020, Rating: 4 stars</b><br/><br/>This is the second instalment in the Truly Devious series.<br/><br/>Ellingham Academy is the dream location for budding creatives, entrepreneurs, geniuses, and innovators. It was also once the setting for an infamous abduction and series of murders. These were solved long ago but for new student Stevie, not accurately enough.<br/><br/>How can Maureen Johnson leave her readers hanging with an ending like that??? Both instalments, in </span>
  <span id="freeText11370717499749459616" style="display:none"><b>First Read: October 2019, Rating: 4 stars<br />Second Read: November 2020, Rating: 4 stars</b><br /><br />This is the second instalment in the Truly Devious series.<br /><br />Ellingham Academy is the dream location for budding creatives, entrepreneurs, geniuses, and innovators. It was also once the setting for an infamous abduction and series of murders. These were solved long ago but for new student Stevie, not accurately enough.<br /><br />How can Maureen Johnson leave her readers hanging with an ending like that??? Both instalments, in this series so far, have been full of all the atmospheric eeriness, compelling mysteries, badass and self-defining characters, and narrative twists that I could desire. I have been continually intrigued and captivated throughout and am both eager and hesitant to see this series through to its end. I have no doubts it will continue to be as thrilling and twisted as all that has already occurred.</span>

<div id="review_2755804470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2755804470" />
    <a title="Clem (the villain&#39;s quest)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68558865-clem-the-villain-s-quest"><img alt="Clem (the villain&#39;s quest)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578041776p2/68558865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2755804470?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clem (the villain&#39;s quest)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clem (the villain&#39;s quest)" href="/user/show/68558865-clem-the-villain-s-quest">Clem (the villain&#39;s quest)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68558865-clem-the-villain-s-quest?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68558865-clem-the-villain-s-quest?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2755804470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4023036981814973024"><i>
  <b>"There's nothing more deceptive than an obvious fact."</b>
</i><br/><br/>⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553355821ra/27255329.gif' width='350' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>GUESS WHO FORGOT TO WRITE THE REVIEW!!</b><br/><br/>Yes, me again, we've been knew. The thing is, that I've read this book a week ago and so many things happened since then that I forgot most of the book due to the fact that I didn't take notes. I was too busy binging The Vanishing Stair to give a fuck. <br/><br/>But here's what I remember. <br/><br/>It's a good book, the writer doesn't take its readers for dumb cunts for a change and the plot was as enticing as </span>
  <span id="freeText4023036981814973024" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"There's nothing more deceptive than an obvious fact."</b>
</i><br><br>⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553355821ra/27255329.gif" width="350" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>GUESS WHO FORGOT TO WRITE THE REVIEW!!</b><br><br>Yes, me again, we've been knew. The thing is, that I've read this book a week ago and so many things happened since then that I forgot most of the book due to the fact that I didn't take notes. I was too busy binging The Vanishing Stair to give a fuck. <br><br>But here's what I remember. <br><br>It's a good book, the writer doesn't take its readers for dumb cunts for a change and the plot was as enticing as the first book's. <br><br>I loved the characters, they're oddballs and while they're not the greatest, I feel like their potential is adequately exploited for a YA novel, especially since it's a thriller with a plot-oriented focus. <br><br>The plot was on point. You could feel the tension in your stomach as the big reveal approached. I knew who had done it due to a haunch but since the writer doesn't give anything away, the reveal scene felt impressive and dramatic. I regret, however, the villain monologue. <br><br>As for the villain, I like the fact that he's not really one. I think that's this book's biggest highlight. I'm so tired of reading people being evil and killing people because they want to. In The Vanishing Stair, what happened was honest to god a mistake, a joke turned which turned sour. You end up pitying the one behind it because it just got beyond his control pretty quickly. It's rare to see a YA that humanizes its antagonist and I stan that. <br><br>The writing style was above average, although it's not outstanding in any way, it made for a fun, spooky at times, novel with a rich universe. I only wished we could have gotten more of the universe but maybe in the next book we will. <br><br><br>That's kind of all I have to say about the Vanishing Stair, it's a great book, I had a great time. My heart was in my throat until the end, waiting for the last twist and turn, and it just kept me hanging with my guess until the end. Can't wait for the third book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4023036981814973024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer16186511469326809052">I was able to get more invested in the story and characters in this book than in book 1, and again the atmosphere are setting are the stars of the show. What I specifically didn't enjoy about this one is that although we are getting real answers, they are just thrown at us by the omnipotent narration, and not revealed due to anything Stevie has done to uncover them. The reader now knows more than anyone else and it's taking away some of the mystery. Regardless, I am finding this series enjoyable</span>
  <span id="freeText16186511469326809052" style="display:none">I was able to get more invested in the story and characters in this book than in book 1, and again the atmosphere are setting are the stars of the show. What I specifically didn't enjoy about this one is that although we are getting real answers, they are just thrown at us by the omnipotent narration, and not revealed due to anything Stevie has done to uncover them. The reader now knows more than anyone else and it's taking away some of the mystery. Regardless, I am finding this series enjoyable. It's very Nancy Drew meets Charlotte Holmes.<br /><br />cw: explosions, dead bodies, claustrophobic spaces</span>

<div id="review_2730196260" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2730196260" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9549139-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595701516p2/9549139.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2730196260?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/9549139-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/39991163-the-vanishing-stair">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9549139-kyle?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9549139-kyle?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2730196260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11353282473881687645">This is bullshit. I cannot stand by another cliffhanger ending, and an author who thinks it’s okay to manipulate their readership into buying another book to find out what happens. This whole series screams “CASH GRAB!”, and I’m done.<br/><br/>I should have been done after book one (which, of course, also ended on a cliffhanger), but more-so because of Maureen Johnson’s clearly biased politics. Now, some may find this to be nit-picking on my part, and maybe a bit overblown, but I need to say it:<br/><br/>It takes a</span>
  <span id="freeText11353282473881687645" style="display:none">This is bullshit. I cannot stand by another cliffhanger ending, and an author who thinks it’s okay to manipulate their readership into buying another book to find out what happens. This whole series screams “CASH GRAB!”, and I’m done.<br /><br />I should have been done after book one (which, of course, also ended on a cliffhanger), but more-so because of Maureen Johnson’s clearly biased politics. Now, some may find this to be nit-picking on my part, and maybe a bit overblown, but I need to say it:<br /><br />It takes a really bitter person to fashion a series around a kidnapping/murder investigation, and make the main villain totally unconnected to that a (although never explicitly confirmed, but glaringly obvious) Republican Senator. A man who is cold, so far as of now unrelated to the central mysteries, and evil for the sake of being the story’s antagonist. We’re never told <i>why</i> he’s a bad guy in any direct way; He’s obviously not a very good father, shady, and has a hidden M.O., but Stevie frequently refers to him as “the devil” and “racist, fascist scum.” This is a person who Stevie blatantly wishes, while on a private plane with the man, was dead— she wonders at the plane crashing, and if the world would be better off if he perished. Like... <i>what the fuck???</i> Even if she were to die as well, she says it would be for the greater good. That is a RADICALIZED, HATEFUL mentality. Everyone in the book has such strong, negative reactions to this Senator, and the fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[David is his son repulses Stevie. Okay, so, you’re saying the guy you like has a <s>Republican</s> father, and that means you cannot like him anymore?? Puhhh-fucking-lease! I continue to love everyone, even if we disagree on things. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And don’t try and tell me that Edward King is never mentioned being a Republican. It does not take a genius to put it together, and here is just another case of a bitter author using her platform to demonize the Republican Party. We’re not all racist, bigoted, xenophobic sheep. What I get from this is that anyone who associates with Republicans is shunned and ostracized. It’s shameful. That’s right— shame on you, Maureen Johnson! The story could’ve been so much better without this plot line. It was unnecessary to what I wanted to read based on the initial blurb from book one.<br /><br />That rant over, I can get back to the book as a whole— but whole, it really isn’t. Splitting up a YA mystery into three books is a strrrretcccchh. And it feels that way. There is so much expository stuff that could have been chopped away, and turned this trilogy into a fairly longer standalone. It would have worked better that way. Even a damn duology would’ve been fine! No more frustrating cliffhangers, and a lot less (if I’m being honest) <b>boring</b> filler.<br /><br />Some random side notes:<br />•A good mystery typically lays most of their cards on the table and begs you to “SOLVE ME (if you can)”. Here, we’re given some clues to start, and then thrown other tidbits of clues at the very end we could never have picked up on. Ever. And again and again, we’re fed more, but it doesn’t feel fun. I want to know the broad strokes, and THEN the smaller details. And we can’t do anything about any of it, even if we knew the answers to some, until Stevie gets it in her head.<br />•David and Stevie are toxic together. I don’t understand the pairing AT ALL!<br />•Again, I found this book too “young” for me. It lacked the hardcore sleuthing I craved, and was pretty “Nancy Drew for the modern age”, but with more hipsters.<br />•I wanted more Nate, Janelle, and Mudge— the only sensible and interesting characters.<br />•I have to give credit for the way Stevie’s anxiety is handled. Props for accurate depictions of panic attacks. Mental illness is no joke... but there is something seriously problematic with David’s behavior, and no one acting on getting him help is sad.<br /><br />I’m done with this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11353282473881687645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

	<tr>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eZAZnuXC8TvkMAlJBu2vgYs6zRuCTrtUXx8QOjusCT0A5Ob4KchC3EOJf85YVfsCMwD+5knxAYaDIg0KjIEqyQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('l9f3DzGjCMtQ5MmLuq+A+9CvexPXfxkono5mN92h1CHuowhp/am7LPddvwzkF9R4aJVI7hzAo/pCs3sHaoz31Q==')})
  }

It was founded by Albert Ellingham, an early twentieth century tycoon, who wanted to make a wonderful place full of riddles, twisting pathways, and gardens. “A place,” he said, “where learning is a game.”\n\nShortly after the school opened, his wife and daughter were kidnapped. The only real clue was a mocking riddle listing methods of murder, signed with the frightening pseudonym “Truly, Devious.” It became one of the great unsolved crimes of American history.\n\nTrue-crime aficionado Stevie Bell is set to begin her first year at Ellingham Academy, and she has an ambitious plan: She will solve this cold case. That is, she will solve the case when she gets a grip on her demanding new school life and her housemates: the inventor, the novelist, the actor, the artist, and the jokester. But something strange is happening. Truly Devious makes a surprise return, and death revisits Ellingham Academy. The past has crawled out of its grave. Someone has gotten away with murder. \n\nThe two interwoven mysteries of this first book in the Truly Devious series dovetail brilliantly, and Stevie Bell will continue her relentless quest for the murderers in books two and three.\n\nNew York Times bestselling author Maureen Johnson weaves a delicate tale of murder and mystery in the first book of a striking new series, perfect for fans of Agatha Christie and E.
